é United States Court of Appeals for the Federal Cirevit handies cases
gubject matter without regard to the region. The Court hears all appeals
the United States Court of Federal Claims, the United States Court of
ternational Trade and the United States Court of Veterans Appeals. The
federal Circuit hears appeals from United States District Courts in patent
ases, cases involving energy regulation and economic stabilization as well
appeals from a variety of administrative proceedings. Established in
82, the Washington, DC-based Federal Circuit possesses national
jurisdiction as a result of the merger between the Appellate Division of the
‘ormer United States Court of Claims and the United States Court of
Slistoms and Patent Appeals.

United States District Court for the Middle District of Alabama 83

 

‘ted States District Courts

jdeval cases are initially tied and decided in the United States
Courts, the federal courts of general trial jurisdiction. There are 94
the 50 states, the District of Columbia, the Commonwealth of
Rico. and the territories of Guam, the United States Virgin islands,
Northen Mariana Islands. With the exception of the territorial

1 district court judges are appointed for life by the President with
ice and consent of the Senate. In each district, the judge who has
on the court the longest and who is under 65 years of age is

ated as the chief judge. The chief judge has administrative duties in
«fo a caseload. Within cach district, the United States Bankruptcy
nears and decides petitions of individuals and businesses seeking
fom bankruptcy. Bankruptcy judges are appointed by the court of

¢ for a term of 14 years. The judges of each district appoint one ot
= magistrate judges, who discharge many of the ancillary duties of the
ict judges. There are both full-time and part-time magistrate judge

1is, and these positions are assigned to the district courts according
easeload criteria. A full-time magistrate judge serves a term of eight
é-'a part-time magistrate judge’s term is four years.
